The pacing of the story is great, almost as soon as you start wondering if there might be too much novelty about the worlds to figure out, something big and recognizable happens and the reader is swept up in the fast pace of events that are understandable and emotionally believable. I loved this book and could not put it down. I'm a big fan of classic space series and have a modes</span>
  <span id="freeText2731142530059837269" style="display:none">Captivating, fast, well-written with characters that hold your attention and interest as soon as you start the book. The pacing of the story is great, almost as soon as you start wondering if there might be too much novelty about the worlds to figure out, something big and recognizable happens and the reader is swept up in the fast pace of events that are understandable and emotionally believable. I loved this book and could not put it down. I'm a big fan of classic space series and have a modest interest in series that rely heavily on psychic phenomenon to explain all manner of action in stories. The combination of the two is a sweet spot, though, and this book does a really nice interpretation especially with the addition of origin stories and fables, which are very creatively designed. As the first book in a series, this promises to be a lot more fun. I received this book as an ARC from Penguin's First to Read program. This was pure joy to read.</span>

<div id="review_929552971" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/929552971" />
    <a title="Erin Arkin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5488337-erin-arkin"><img alt="Erin Arkin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1306457942p2/5488337.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/929552971?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin Arkin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin Arkin" href="/user/show/5488337-erin-arkin">Erin Arkin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5488337-erin-arkin?shelf=i-have-a-real-book">i-have-a-real-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5488337-erin-arkin?shelf=galley-arc">galley-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5488337-erin-arkin?shelf=bea">bea</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5488337-erin-arkin?shelf=2014-real-book-challenge">2014-real-book-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer929552971" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2585305701811203417">Zodiac by Romina Russell was a solid four stars for me. I found it full of action and the space travel and science fiction aspect only added to the story. I won't be saying a ton about the details of this book only because I don't want to give anything away - apologies but I don't want to spoil it!<br/><br/>Russell built the structure of the space system and the planets so that it was easy to create a picture in my mind of the world these characters live in. I loved the space travel and the differences be</span>
  <span id="freeText2585305701811203417" style="display:none">Zodiac by Romina Russell was a solid four stars for me. I found it full of action and the space travel and science fiction aspect only added to the story. I won't be saying a ton about the details of this book only because I don't want to give anything away - apologies but I don't want to spoil it!<br /><br />Russell built the structure of the space system and the planets so that it was easy to create a picture in my mind of the world these characters live in. I loved the space travel and the differences between each of the twelve houses…and the mystery surrounding the mythical 13th house. <br /><br />Rho is an interesting character and I liked her. I have to admit, I was frustrated with some of the decisions she made but she made those decisions with the right intentions…in most cases, I think. As she is thrown into a life she never imagined she jumps right in and embraces all aspects. The thing that stands out for me about Rho is the fact that she never changes her point of view on what is really going on regardless of what people are telling her. This is most evident when she is trying to figure out if she should hide her belief of Ophiuchus and the fact that he is the one attacking the houses.<br /><br />I thought that both Mathias and Dysan were solid characters as well. They were almost complete opposites of each other but when it came to Rho, they both cared a lot about her and were willing to do whatever they could to keep her safe. I’m not going to say too much about these two as I don’t want to give anything away but I will warn you, if it isn’t clear, there is a bit of a love triangle. With that said, it doesn’t take over the story but it does flow through the book and plays a part in some of the decisions made.<br /><br />As Rho tries to navigate the politics of being Guardian of House Cancer as well as figuring out how to get everyone to see how much danger they are in, she is also faced with the potential loss of her family and has to figure out how to keep going without know where they are or if they are safe. <br /><br />I can’t really say too much about the rest of the story as I don’t want to give anything away but I think the bigger mysteries still exist around Ophiuchus and Rho’s mother. I felt like we – just like Rho – don’t know what happened to her mother and I have a feeling there is still something to be revealed about her. As for Ophiuchus, there is more to come…I know it and I can’t wait to see where Russell goes with that part of the story. <br /><br />Russell created a wonderful story with a unique spin around the zodiac and as soon as I picked it up, I had a hard time putting it down. I'm absolutely looking forward to the next book in the series and if you are looking for a new Dystopian/Science Fiction series, definitely consider checking this one out.<br /><br />Thank you to the publisher for the review copy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2585305701811203417" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13300542417716972785"><i>Zodiac</i>, a bestselling fantasy/sci-fi YA, is in a whole different galaxy from where my eyes usually roam, but I've enjoyed buddy reading it by phone with a teen whose school is closed for the year by coronavirus.<br/><br/>Sixteen-year-old Acolyte Rhoma Grace attends the Zodai Academy on Elara, Cancer's largest moon, and is playing a gig with her band when a fireball blows up Thebes, another moon where her brother Stanton works, triggering devastation throughout the Cancrian constellation.<br/><br/>In the aftermath, </span>
  <span id="freeText13300542417716972785" style="display:none"><i>Zodiac</i>, a bestselling fantasy/sci-fi YA, is in a whole different galaxy from where my eyes usually roam, but I've enjoyed buddy reading it by phone with a teen whose school is closed for the year by coronavirus.<br /><br />Sixteen-year-old Acolyte Rhoma Grace attends the Zodai Academy on Elara, Cancer's largest moon, and is playing a gig with her band when a fireball blows up Thebes, another moon where her brother Stanton works, triggering devastation throughout the Cancrian constellation.<br /><br />In the aftermath, Rho is called upon to lead Cancer and to warn the rest of the Zodiac against Ophiuchus, vengeful Guardian of what has been thought to be a mythical 13th House, who launched the attack on Cancer and appears intent on destroying the whole galaxy. As she negotiates this new role thrust upon her, she's also conflicted by new feelings about both her bodyguard, Lodestar Mathias Thais, and Libran Ambassador Hysan Dax.<br /><br />Romina Russell has created a marvelous world, with the peoples of each constellation reflecting different characteristics associated with their astrological profiles, and imaginative technologies and nomenclature, e.g. the drug Abyssthe. The writing is compelling and the pages fly by.<br /><br />I'm looking forward to exploring the next book in this series, <i>Wandering Star</i>.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20821306.Zodiac__Zodiac___1_" title="Zodiac (Zodiac, #1) by Romina Russell" rel="nofollow noopener">Zodiac</a></span>

    <a title="Gergana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312798-gergana"><img alt="Gergana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1439319393p2/5312798.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1129829601" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16182732163201957958">Read on January 05, 2016, DNF 30%<br/>Booooooook! Why, boooook? I liked you! I waited for you for months. I had a crush on you ever since I saw your gorgeous cover on goodreads, and when I read your synopsis, it was like it was meant to be! We were perfect for eachother (I'm a Cancer too) and my heart practically skipped a beat when I saw you in the bookstore. It was insta love! Why did you have to be so.... so... so the extreme opposite of awesome?<br/><br/>Honestly, this book was <b>so not for me</b> that I don't f</span>
  <span id="freeText16182732163201957958" style="display:none">Read on January 05, 2016, DNF 30%<br />Booooooook! Why, boooook? I liked you! I waited for you for months. I had a crush on you ever since I saw your gorgeous cover on goodreads, and when I read your synopsis, it was like it was meant to be! We were perfect for eachother (I'm a Cancer too) and my heart practically skipped a beat when I saw you in the bookstore. It was insta love! Why did you have to be so.... so... so the extreme opposite of awesome?<br /><br />Honestly, this book was <b>so not for me</b> that I don't feel like I have the right to bad-mouth it. You like YA with all its clichés (special snowflake, insta love, love triangle, bland and boring heroine, etc.) go for it. My mistake was that I expected a sci-fi novel, instead of an angsty teen drama with a Mary Sue who is always right and perfect, but never taken seriously by the idiotic adults. And all boys fall for her, cause she's just too beautiful and dumb. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16182732163201957958" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1059583539" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1059583539" />
    <a title="Frank Chillura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34993279-frank-chillura"><img alt="Frank Chillura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410838626p2/34993279.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1059583539?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Frank Chillura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Frank Chillura" href="/user/show/34993279-frank-chillura">Frank Chillura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34993279-frank-chillura?shelf=astrology">astrology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34993279-frank-chillura?shelf=space-travel">space-travel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1059583539" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12647397941399450455">So, it is pretty late & I only just got home from seeing The Maze Runner in theaters... so I am still buzzing from that. I am happy I am finally getting to write my review for Zodiac, because I have been reading it now for a few days & have really been dying to let everyone know what I think.<br/><br/>Zodiac is a very complex story about many things. It is about strength, courage, building your world back after losing everything you once knew & loved. It is about making new alliances with people you do no</span>
  <span id="freeText12647397941399450455" style="display:none">So, it is pretty late &amp; I only just got home from seeing The Maze Runner in theaters... so I am still buzzing from that. I am happy I am finally getting to write my review for Zodiac, because I have been reading it now for a few days &amp; have really been dying to let everyone know what I think.<br /><br />Zodiac is a very complex story about many things. It is about strength, courage, building your world back after losing everything you once knew &amp; loved. It is about making new alliances with people you do not know... it is about so many things that I find it hard to believe that anyone reading it would not be able to find something about it they loved. <br /><br />Each of the 12 houses of the Zodiac have a quality that they personify.<br /><br />Aries: Military<br /><br />Virgo: Sustenance<br /><br />Scorpio: Innovation<br /><br />Capricorn: Wisdom<br /><br />Gemini: Imagination<br /><br />Pisces: Spirituality<br /><br />Taurus: Industry<br /><br />Libra: Justice<br /><br />Aquarius: Philosophy<br /><br />Sagittarius: Curiosity<br /><br />Leo: Passion<br /><br />Cancer: Nurture<br /><br />Every human living on 1 of the 12 planets in this solar system (which are named for each of the signs of the zodiac) live by that one word or belief. <br /><br />I have loved &amp; enjoyed this book thoroughly. I find that many great YA books that I end up remembering or loving the most have that Love Triangle going where you are always rooting for one person to come out on top. At certain times I was rooting for one and at other times the other. That does not happen unless there is really great story telling happening. <br /><br />I hope I have given you enough information to pick up a copy of this book when it is released, because I want everyone to love it as much as I have.<br /><br />If you are looking for any other book or series suggestions, feel free to message me through my blog UtopiaNeverComes.blogspot.com or email me at FooFiFauxPaw@google.com.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12647397941399450455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_872551316" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/872551316" />
    <a title="Paige (Illegal in 3 Countries)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27556706-paige-illegal-in-3-countries"><img alt="Paige (Illegal in 3 Countries)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389396084p2/27556706.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/872551316?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paige (Illegal in 3 Countries)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paige (Illegal in 3 Countries)" href="/user/show/27556706-paige-illegal-in-3-countries">Paige (Illegal in 3 Countries)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27556706-paige-illegal-in-3-countries?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27556706-paige-illegal-in-3-countries?shelf=bea-2014">bea-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27556706-paige-illegal-in-3-countries?shelf=series-unfinished">series-unfinished</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer872551316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7712566000950222633">See more of my reviews on <a href='http://theyakitten.net' rel='nofollow noopener'>The YA Kitten</a>! My copy was an ARC I got at BEA 2014.<br/><br/>I may not read my horoscopes or put any faith in those things, but the zodiac and all that is one of my favorite things to study. Even if the horoscopes are inaccurate, my personality fits my sign (WHOOOOO CAPRICORN) far more than any other and it works for my friends too. A sci-fi fantasy series that takes the signs and makes them into their own constellations fighting against the evils of Ochus? YES PLEASE. Well, it </span>
  <span id="freeText7712566000950222633" style="display:none">See more of my reviews on <a href="http://theyakitten.net" rel="nofollow noopener">The YA Kitten</a>! My copy was an ARC I got at BEA 2014.<br /><br />I may not read my horoscopes or put any faith in those things, but the zodiac and all that is one of my favorite things to study. Even if the horoscopes are inaccurate, my personality fits my sign (WHOOOOO CAPRICORN) far more than any other and it works for my friends too. A sci-fi fantasy series that takes the signs and makes them into their own constellations fighting against the evils of Ochus? YES PLEASE. Well, it turned out to be a NOPE instead. Zodiac is a two-dimensional book that leaves you with more questions than answers–and something tells me most of those questions will never be answered.<br /><br />Rhoma should be a solid main character who takes action when she realizes how much danger everyone is in, but she’s not. Sure, she does exactly what I described above, but readers don’t really know her. They just know what traits she has as a Cancrian because it’s described into infinity. Not everyone will fit their sign to a T; Capricorns are supposed to be patient and resistant to impulsive behavior, but I’m impatient as can be and impulsive decisions are my only decisions. That Rho is never given any depth beyond her house traits weakens her ability to carry this book.<br /><br />Furthermore, Rho’s odd reactions to certain revelations make her character that much harder to bond with. The entire prologue is her mother infodumping the idea of Ochus and how he approached each constellation in a different form. A little while later, the same information is repeated and Rho is surprised. Didn’t she already know this? Then when someone tells her that her long-missing mother has committed treason, Rho reacts not to her mother’s sudden reappearance but to the idea a Cancrian would commit treason. It’s obvious her mom will have an important role to play in this series, but nothing is done with her this installment.<br /><br />These characterization issue plagues the entire novel. Readers know characters not by their individual personalities but by what traits they say they have as a member of House Whatever. The zodiac houses and their associated traits are used as characterization shortcuts and take over a character instead of supplementing their personality. Don’t ask me to count how many times someone talks about what kind of person they are through the invocation of a house trait because we’re going to need some pretty high numbers for it. These are just two examples:<br /><br /><blockquote>Treason.<br /><br />The word sounds strange, unconnected to my life. “I don’t believe you.” It’s almost a snarl. “Betrayal is not in our Cancrian nature.” (p. 38, ARC)</blockquote><br /><br />And:<br /><br /><blockquote>“I know we Sagittarians can be conspiracy nuts at times, but Rho, if someone from the Thirteenth House is behind this, and all these tragedies are part of a trajectory–from the disasters on Leo and Taurus to what’s happened on your moons–they’re also altering history to cover their tracks.” (p. 65-66, ARC)</blockquote><br /><br />Since I’m quoting things, have this bonus of Eyes Don’t Work Like That:<br /><br /><blockquote>“His eyes are dimming, growing light as air, until he’s so far removed from this moment that the only visible part of his right iris is the golden star.” (p. 304, ARC)</blockquote><br /><br />Another problem with the other characters in the novel comes from how some of them are described. Rho’s friend Nishi (full name Nishiko Sai, so obviously Japanese-but-not) is described as having cinnamon skin and exotic beauty; people from House Taurus are noted for having complexions that range from “creamy camel to dark cocoa” and I’m not sure if that descriptions intends to say “caramel” or actually means camel. Either way, <a href="http://t.co/6SzOD0B0f5" rel="nofollow noopener">describing characters of color in terms of food is really problematic</a>. Setting this novel in the far, far future in a fictional galaxy doesn’t remove such horrific implications from those descriptions. JUST STOP DOING IT, OKAY?<br /><br />The weak love triangle made weaker by threadbare characterization is the final nail in the coffin. One whines that they can’t be together because he’s too old for her (WHOOP-DEE-DO, FIVE YEARS’ AGE DIFFERENCE) and the other is Adrian-from-Vampire-Academy-like with none of the charisma and depth. Somehow, Rho is torn between them when she never develops relationships of any kind with either man. The tragic fate of one of them isn’t even tragic. Number one rule of death in fiction: they’re not dead until you see the body yourself. (I’ll leave the rest unspecified. You’ll have to find out from someone else what happens to who!)<br /><br />As with many zodiac-focused books, the question of people who have one sign and act like another isn’t addressed solidly. They get all of two paragraphs before they’re brushed off even though following the birth date rule that governs zodiac assignment means ninety percent of each system’s population would be Risers.The explanation is so short and leaves so many questions unanswered that it bears more quoting:<br /><br /><blockquote>A Riser is a person born into the wrong house. It’s a change that happens when a person’s exterior persona conflicts so strongly with their internal identity that they begin to develop the personality and physical traits of a different house. And it can happen at any age.<br /><br /> Most people handle it well and either choose to stay on their home planets and continue living their lives, or move to the House that reflects their rising persona. There are rare cases where the change doesn’t take well, and a Riser can have an unbalanced ratio of personality traits from their old and new Houses. Sometimes it deforms them. Sometimes it turns them into monsters. (p. 212, ARC)</blockquote><br /><br />The idea an entire planet of people will grow up to behave like Cancers even if they’re born under every sign but cancer is simply unbelievable–and the irony of the idea this is what I get hung up about this book on doesn’t escape me. My suspension of disbelief is a strange thing. These poor Divergents, probably turned into monsters because their own people treated them like freaks for being born on a Gemini planet but acting like a Leo.<br /><br />Back in my junior year of high school, I had an idea for a magical realism epic focused on the zodiac. I only ever wrote the first chapter of it, but so much thought went into it that with the help of a few travel books for various countries, I could jump right in. Russell put even more thought into her world than I put into mine, but it still comes out unsatisfying. The details are there for each planet–mostly on the series website, which is one giant encyclopedia–but there’s still so much that isn’t explained at all or explained sensibly. I know what an Ephemeris is, but I don’t understand it. Science terms are thrown around and Capitalized Words are everywhere. If you want to get a deeper understanding of them, you’re out of luck. You just have to take them at face value.<br /><br />Is there anything nice I can say about this book? Sadly, no. I admire this novel more for its potential and the thought put into it, not what it really is. Its logic may be flawed and forgot to consider a few important factors, but the idea is why I kept reading despite my dissatisfaction. That would be why it’s safe from my lowest ratings.<br /><br />I referred to it as #ZodiACK for more than one reason while reading it, as you can see. This book needs to give readers so much more than it does, but if it wants to save the decent stuff for future books, go ahead. I’m out. I can only recommend this to readers who loved Divergent wholeheartedly and saw no holes or problems with its worldbuilding whatsoever. However, I do recommend checking out <a href="http://zodiacbooks.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">the series website</a> because it gave me plenty of laughs. I come from Capricorn, the socialist system! Taurus is run like a corporation! That will never not be funny. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7712566000950222633" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1144577344" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1144577344" />
    <a title="desirey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38467269-desirey"><img alt="desirey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517610083p2/38467269.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1144577344?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="desirey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="desirey" href="/user/show/38467269-desirey">desirey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1144577344" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8868328273849486380">With an action packed story line, a dynamic set of characters, and a world that is uniquely crafted by the author's imagination, Zodiac is a brilliant book that keeps you wondering what will happen next.<br/><br/>Romina brings to life a strong protagonist who you will be cheering for as soon as you read the first page. Rhoma Grace, from House Cancer, wants to unite the 12 Houses together and warn them of the danger approaching among the planets. She tells them that the 13th House isn't a myth, but they do</span>
  <span id="freeText8868328273849486380" style="display:none">With an action packed story line, a dynamic set of characters, and a world that is uniquely crafted by the author's imagination, Zodiac is a brilliant book that keeps you wondering what will happen next.<br /><br />Romina brings to life a strong protagonist who you will be cheering for as soon as you read the first page. Rhoma Grace, from House Cancer, wants to unite the 12 Houses together and warn them of the danger approaching among the planets. She tells them that the 13th House isn't a myth, but they don't believe her. While she is trying to bring the divided Houses together, she also has to worry about her job. She is a Guardian who wants to help not only her House, but all 12 of them because she doesn't want to see them fall. <br /><br />She has two friends helping her: Hysan Dax, from House Libra, and Mathias, a major in the Cancrian Guard. They travel to different Houses in hope the others will listen to her about the 13th House that she suspects is the reason behind all the strange weather that's been happening. <br /><br />Zodiac is 319 pages, and even though I wish it was more, it's still a wonderful and intriguing read. It's fast paced and the author knows how to keep you on the edge of your seat. You can tell the author worked hard to weave this story together and has an incredible imagination. She created an unique world with 12 Houses, each one beautifully crafted with history, culture, and fashion. The scenery is rich and vivid that you feel like you are right there along Rhoma cheering her on in the midst of space. <br /><br />You can't help but grow to care for each of these characters to the point where you don't want to see any of them getting hurt. Rhoma was definitely one of my favorite characters of the story, so heroic and selfless, I can't wait to read more about her in this series. The ending will leave you with several different emotions. There's so much suspense and all I want is to see Rhoma and the characters have a happy ending. <br /><br />If you love a story that keeps you on the edge of your seat, a story of science-fiction, love, friendship, and hope, as well as a strong protagonist with a good reason worth fighting for, this is a story worth reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8868328273849486380" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2038268849" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2038268849" />
    <a title="Krysti" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12625388-krysti"><img alt="Krysti" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582829417p2/12625388.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2038268849?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krysti" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krysti" href="/user/show/12625388-krysti">Krysti</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2038268849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4256463467435781766">I am so enthralled by the world that Romina Russell has created in Zodiac. She has beautifully combined science fiction and astrology to craft a setting that is every bit as breathtaking as this gorgeous book cover.<br/><br/>The characters are divided into separate houses based on the zodiac signs, and the common attributes of those signs manifest themselves in the characters' traits and strengths, which is such a fun and original approach to character development.<br/><br/>The plot is incredibly fast paced and hig</span>
  <span id="freeText4256463467435781766" style="display:none">I am so enthralled by the world that Romina Russell has created in Zodiac. She has beautifully combined science fiction and astrology to craft a setting that is every bit as breathtaking as this gorgeous book cover.<br /><br />The characters are divided into separate houses based on the zodiac signs, and the common attributes of those signs manifest themselves in the characters' traits and strengths, which is such a fun and original approach to character development.<br /><br />The plot is incredibly fast paced and high-stakes right from the very beginning. When tragedy forces Rhoma into an unpredicted position of power, readers get to see behind the scenes of the political machinations taking place in this world, which is very intriguing and helps balance out some of the intense action scenes that occur throughout the story.<br /><br />Yes. There is a love triangle in this story. I personally am not a hater of love triangles in novels as long as they make sense and work well within the story, and I do feel that that was the case in Zodiac. There is some sizzling romantic tension between Rhoma and both Hysan and Mathias. I found the dynamic between the three of them scintillating and so much fun to read.<br /><br />I also love me a good villain, and Zodiac has an excellent villain. Russel does a good job of showing his treachery while hinting at the motivations behind his actions.<br /><br />Overall, I really enjoyed this story. I found it entertaining and imaginative and really enjoyed the dazzling setting it took place in. I'm so looking forward to the next book in our readathon, Wandering Star, and hope you'll join us!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4256463467435781766" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4205963-rachel-kulik?shelf=2015">2015</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1104995825" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15301992598039963593"><b>This review is posted on my blog <a href='http://rachelreading.wordpress.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rachel Reading</a>. If you like this, and would like to see more like it, please check it out!</b><br/><br/>This book is more like 4.75. I rounded up.<br/><br/>WELL HOLY SHIT BALLS this book was good. It was real good. And I feel like I disagree with a lot of the people who think this is just another love triangle gone wrong kind of thing. This book has some of the MOST AMAZING world building I’ve ever seen, and maybe that’s because I was obsessed with astrology for a really really long tim</span>
  <span id="freeText15301992598039963593" style="display:none"><b>This review is posted on my blog <a href="http://rachelreading.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Rachel Reading</a>. If you like this, and would like to see more like it, please check it out!</b><br /><br />This book is more like 4.75. I rounded up.<br /><br />WELL HOLY SHIT BALLS this book was good. It was real good. And I feel like I disagree with a lot of the people who think this is just another love triangle gone wrong kind of thing. This book has some of the MOST AMAZING world building I’ve ever seen, and maybe that’s because I was obsessed with astrology for a really really long time. It did take me awhile to get through this book, but it was so worth it.<br /><br />I needed to finish a book and I’m so glad I finally committed to this one. The ending was crazy, and despite some weird awkward lines when it came to love, there was also some amazing parts as well. I love Rho’s movement in the book, and after that ending, I can’t wait to see what’s next. OBSESSED.</span>

  <span id="freeText12157676305108040587" style="display:none">OBSESSED! <br />This book creates impressive worlds with very dynamic characters! The details Romina comes us with throughout the book are mind-blowing. For example, the different Ophiuchus stories and how each House represents qualities from each of the Zodiac signs.<br />I don't want to spoil this book for anyone who hasn't read it, but I totally went through multiple emotions while reading it.   function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Vz7uAzQW1wjyh8LdcAYFlclR0LzV4Q/zcPbTBCTRNG0R2l2P/8HoKueYQ3weanZAlQr6TXGrNqiaJSi0BflMYw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZDvmPG7WsvuvyjKVZirAEQ+Vj3Ww18HsCekIfkTt/R4i31WwpQGN2brVszQIRrPEU86lhBSd+LfjOvPOZcWFEA==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer18026946550177878846">Romina Russell (aka Romina Garber) is a Los Angeles based author who originally hails from Buenos Aires, Argentina. As a teen, Romina landed her first writing gig—College She Wrote, a weekly Sunday column for the Miami Herald that was later picked up for national syndication—and she hasn’t stopped writing since. When she’s not working on ZODIAC, Romina can be found producing movie trailers, taking</span>
  <span id="freeText18026946550177878846" style="display:none">Romina Russell (aka Romina Garber) is a Los Angeles based author who originally hails from Buenos Aires, Argentina. As a teen, Romina landed her first writing gig—College She Wrote, a weekly Sunday column for the Miami Herald that was later picked up for national syndication—and she hasn’t stopped writing since. When she’s not working on ZODIAC, Romina can be found producing movie trailers, taking photographs, or daydreaming about buying a new drum set. She is a graduate of Harvard College and a Virgo to the core.</span>

        first.parentNode.insertBefore(script, first);
      }
    }
  if (w.attachEvent) {
    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
    ['//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js',
     '//apis.google.com/js/plusone.js'
    ]
  ));

//]]>
</script>

      </div>
